class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Hip hop</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">

<li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queen_Bee_Entertainment" title="Queen Bee Entertainment">Queen Bee</a></li>

<li>Undeas</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Junior_M.A.F.I.A." title="Junior M.A.F.I.A.">Junior M.A.F.I.A.</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kimberly Denise Jones</b> (born July 11, 1974),<sup id="cite_ref-:3_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> better known by her stage name <b>Lil' Kim</b>, is an American rapper and singer. She was born and raised in New York City and lived much of her adolescent life on the streets after being expelled from home. In her teens, she would <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle rap</a>, influenced by fellow female hip-hop artists like <a href="/wiki/MC_Lyte" title="MC Lyte">MC Lyte</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Lady_of_Rage" title="The Lady of Rage">the Lady of Rage</a>. In 1994, she was discovered by fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, who invited her to join his group <a href="/wiki/Junior_M.A.F.I.A." title="Junior M.A.F.I.A.">Junior M.A.F.I.A.</a>; their debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(Junior_M.A.F.I.A._album)" title="Conspiracy (Junior M.A.F.I.A. album)">Conspiracy</a>,</i> generated two top 20 singles in the United States and was <a href="/wiki/Gold_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold certification">certified gold</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).
</p><p>Lil' Kim's debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Hard_Core_(Lil%27_Kim_album)" title="Hard Core (Lil&#39; Kim album)">Hard Core</a></i> (1996) was certified <a href="/wiki/Platinum_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Platinum certification">double platinum</a> in March 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Since its release, it has sold more than six million copies worldwide<sup id="cite_ref-dazeed_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dazeed-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and spawned three successful singles: "<a href="/wiki/No_Time_(Lil%27_Kim_song)" title="No Time (Lil&#39; Kim song)">No Time</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Not_Tonight_(song)" title="Not Tonight (song)">Not Tonight (Ladies Night)</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/Crush_on_You_(Lil%27_Kim_song)" title="Crush on You (Lil&#39; Kim song)">Crush on You</a>." <i>Hard Core</i> had the highest debut in the US for a female rap album at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Her following albums, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_K.I.M." title="The Notorious K.I.M.">The Notorious K.I.M.</a></i> (2000) and <i><a href="/wiki/La_Bella_Mafia" title="La Bella Mafia">La Bella Mafia</a></i> (2003) were also certified platinum. In 2001, Lil' Kim reached number one on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> with the single "<a href="/wiki/Lady_Marmalade#Moulin_Rouge!_version" title="Lady Marmalade">Lady Marmalade</a>" (a remake of <a href="/wiki/Lady_Marmalade" title="Lady Marmalade">LaBelle's 1974 single</a>), alongside <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BDa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mýa">Mýa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>. Other notable singles from this period include "<a href="/wiki/The_Jump_Off" title="The Jump Off">The Jump Off</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Magic_Stick_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic Stick (song)">Magic Stick</a>," the latter of which reached number two on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, becoming her 2nd-highest-charting single as a lead artist.
</p><p>In 2005, Lil' Kim served a one-year prison sentence for <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">lying to a jury</a> about her friends' involvement in a shooting four years earlier. During her incarceration, her fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Naked_Truth_(Lil%27_Kim_album)" title="The Naked Truth (Lil&#39; Kim album)">The Naked Truth</a>,</i> was released to positive reviews from critics. A reality series covering her sentence, <i><a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim:_Countdown_to_Lockdown" title="Lil&#39; Kim: Countdown to Lockdown">Lil' Kim: Countdown to Lockdown</a>,</i> premiered on <a href="/wiki/BET" title="BET">BET</a> in 2006. She then released her first mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Ms._G.O.A.T." title="Ms. G.O.A.T.">Ms. G.O.A.T.</a></i> (2008) and returned to the public eye in 2009 with an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a>.</i> Throughout the 2010s, she continued to release music and perform sporadically, collaborating with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>. Her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/9_(Lil%27_Kim_album)" title="9 (Lil&#39; Kim album)">9</a>,</i> was released in 2019.
</p><p>Lil' Kim has been referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music#L" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Rap</a>," as well as her alias "Queen Bee" by several media outlets. She has sold more than 15 million albums and 30 million singles worldwide. Her songs "No Time," "Big Momma Thang," and "Not Tonight (Ladies Night)" were each listed on <a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)"><i>Complex</i></a>'s list of the 50 Best Rap Songs By Women.<sup id="cite_ref-The_50_Best_Rap_Songs_by_Women_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_50_Best_Rap_Songs_by_Women-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, she was listed on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Greatest Women in Music list at number 45, the second-highest position for a solo female hip-hop artist.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Aside from music, she is also known for her risk-taking and luxurious approach to fashion which has inspired many artists; she has been cited as a <a href="/wiki/Fashion_icons" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion icons">fashion icon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She has been noted for helping women embrace their "sexuality and femininity" in a way that was a stark contrast at the time from other female artists.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span id="Early_life.2C_family_and_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life,_family_and_education">Early life, family and education</span></h2>
<p>Jones was born in the <a href="/wiki/Bedford%E2%80%93Stuyvesant,_Brooklyn" title="Bedford–Stuyvesant, Brooklyn">Bedford–Stuyvesant</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, the second child of Linwood Jones, a former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U.S. Marine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> She has an older brother, Christopher.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> As a child, Jones attended <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_All_Saints_Church_(Brooklyn,_New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of All Saints Church (Brooklyn, New York)">Queen of All Saints Elementary School</a> in Brooklyn.<sup id="cite_ref-bio.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> When she was nine years old, her parents separated, and Jones was raised by her father, with whom she had a tumultuous relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-bio.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> At fourteen, she left home, began living on the streets, and ended up dropping out of high school.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a teenager, Jones met Christopher Wallace, known professionally as <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">the Notorious B.I.G.</a>, who was a key figure in both her personal and artistic life, particularly after Wallace gained popularity and influence through his relationship with <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean "Puffy" Combs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Jones attended Sarah J. Hale Vocational High School for two-and-a-half years. Many of her friends also went there, and they would all often skip school together. Since she was not completing her schoolwork, the decision was made for her to transfer to <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_College_Academy" title="Brooklyn College Academy">Brooklyn College Academy</a> to finish her remaining year and a half of high school.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This was the same school that fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(rapper)" title="Foxy Brown (rapper)">Foxy Brown</a> attended.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<p>In 1994, B.I.G. was instrumental in introducing and promoting the Brooklyn-based group <a href="/wiki/Junior_M.A.F.I.A." title="Junior M.A.F.I.A.">Junior M.A.F.I.A</a>. Jones, who had adopted the <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage name</a> Lil' Kim, was a member of the group. The group's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(Junior_M.A.F.I.A._album)" title="Conspiracy (Junior M.A.F.I.A. album)">Conspiracy</a>,</i> was released to mediocre reviews and moderate sales on August 29, 1995, but debuted at number eight on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 69,000 copies in its first week of release. Wallace wrote and <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwrote</a> most of the album's material.<sup id="cite_ref-hardcoresales_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hardcoresales-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Three hit singles came from <i>Conspiracy</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Player%27s_Anthem" title="Player&#39;s Anthem">Player's Anthem</a>," "<a href="/wiki/I_Need_You_Tonight_(Junior_M.A.F.I.A._song)" title="I Need You Tonight (Junior M.A.F.I.A. song)">I Need You Tonight</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/Get_Money_(Junior_M.A.F.I.A._song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Get Money (Junior M.A.F.I.A. song)">Get Money</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">RIAA certified</a> <i>Conspiracy</i> a Gold album on December 6, 1995. "Player's Anthem" and "Get Money" were certified gold and platinum respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim's increasing popularity as a member of Junior M.A.F.I.A. allowed her to start a solo career shortly after the <i>Conspiracy</i> album was released. By late 1995, she began working on what would become her debut album, <i>Hard Core.</i>
</p>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.932002:_Hard_Core_and_The_Notorious_K.I.M."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–2002:_Hard_Core_and_The_Notorious_K.I.M.">1996–2002: <i>Hard Core</i> and <i>The Notorious K.I.M.</i></span></h3>
<p>After a year with Junior M.A.F.I.A., Lil' Kim began her solo career by making guest performances on R&amp;B albums and recording her debut album, <i>Hard Core</i>, which was released in November 1996. The album debuted at number 11 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, the highest debut for a female rap album at that time,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and number 3 on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-albums_charts_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albums_charts-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> selling 78,000 copies in its first week of release and has sold over 5 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-hardcoresales_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hardcoresales-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> It was certified double platinum by the RIAA on March 14, 2001, after having been certified gold on January 6, 1997, and platinum on June 3, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's lead single "<a href="/wiki/No_Time_(Lil%27_Kim_song)" title="No Time (Lil&#39; Kim song)">No Time</a>," a duet with Combs, reached the top spot of the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Songs" title="Hot Rap Songs">Hot Rap Tracks</a> chart<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and was certified gold by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The following single was "<a href="/wiki/Crush_on_You_(Lil%27_Kim_song)" title="Crush on You (Lil&#39; Kim song)">Crush on You</a>," a remixed version of the track that appeared on Hard Core. A remix of the album's track "Not Tonight" saw Lil' Kim team up with <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angie_Martinez" title="Angie Martinez">Angie Martinez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Da_Brat" title="Da Brat">Da Brat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Lopes" title="Lisa Lopes">Left Eye</a> of <a href="/wiki/TLC_(group)" title="TLC (group)">TLC</a> with the song peaking at 6 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The song was part of <a href="/wiki/Nothing_to_Lose_(soundtrack)" title="Nothing to Lose (soundtrack)">the soundtrack</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lawrence" title="Martin Lawrence">Martin Lawrence</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Nothing_to_Lose_(1997_film)" title="Nothing to Lose (1997 film)">Nothing to Lose</a>,</i> nominated for a Grammy Award, and certified platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> She became the first female rapper to have three consecutive number ones on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Rap Tracks chart.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In one stockholders' meeting of <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>, activist <a href="/wiki/C._Delores_Tucker" title="C. Delores Tucker">C. Delores Tucker</a> criticized the label "for producing this filth," referring to perceived graphic sexual content in Lil' Kim's lyrics, and labeling them "gangsta porno rap."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, Lil' Kim promoted <i>Hard Core</i> by performing on P. Diddy's "No Way Out" tour.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The tour continued through to 1998 and became one of the highest-grossing hip-hop tours of all time, grossing an estimated $16 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Group2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Group2007-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> That same year, she launched her own label, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Bee_Entertainment" title="Queen Bee Entertainment">Queen Bee Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Mask_of_Lil&#39;_Kim_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Mask_of_Lil&#39;_Kim-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1998 to 2000, Lil' Kim continued working under the management of B.I.G.'s best friend, Damion "D-Roc" Butler's "Roc Management," touring and modeling for various fashion and pop culture companies including <a href="/wiki/Candie%27s" title="Candie&#39;s">Candie's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace_S.p.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Gianni Versace S.p.A.">Versace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceberg_(fashion_house)" title="Iceberg (fashion house)">Iceberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baby_Phat" title="Baby Phat">Baby Phat</a>. Her outfit at the <a href="/wiki/1999_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1999 MTV Video Music Awards">1999 MTV Video Music Awards</a> received widespread media attention, fueled by the "shocked" response of presenter <a href="/wiki/Diana_Ross" title="Diana Ross">Diana Ross</a>, who approached and jiggled Kim's exposed breast on national television. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> considered that the incident solidified Lil' Kim's "image of sexual fearlessness" and her career as "a fashion trendsetter."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Mask_of_Lil&#39;_Kim_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Mask_of_Lil&#39;_Kim-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 27, 2000, Lil' Kim released her second album, <i>The Notorious K.I.M.</i> The album marked a new image and revamped look for the rapper. Despite the limited success of its singles, the album debuted at number 4 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and number 1 on the Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums chart, selling 229,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-hardcoresales_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hardcoresales-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> It was certified platinum by the RIAA, four weeks after its release.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It was on this LP that the well-known hip-hop feud between Lil' Kim and Foxy Brown escalated. In 2001, Lil' Kim teamed up with Christina Aguilera, Pink, and Mýa to remake "Lady Marmalade," which was originally written about a <a href="/wiki/Brothel" title="Brothel">bordello</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> and performed by the group <a href="/wiki/Labelle" title="Labelle">Labelle</a> (which included diva <a href="/wiki/Patti_LaBelle" title="Patti LaBelle">Patti LaBelle</a>) 25 years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The song was recorded for the <i><a href="/wiki/Moulin_Rouge!" title="Moulin Rouge!">Moulin Rouge!</a></i> film soundtrack, released in April 2001, and stayed at number 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for five weeks. The song also went to number 1 in 50 countries around the world. This was a major accomplishment for female rap, as well as for Lil' Kim, who scored her first number 1 Hot 100 hit<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and became the second solo female rapper in history to hit number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 charts.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"Lady Marmalade" also garnered Lil' Kim her first Grammy Award. The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Kimnotyze" title="Kimnotyze">Kimnotyze</a>," was released as the lead single of record producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Tomekk" title="DJ Tomekk">DJ Tomekk</a>'s compilation album <i>Beat Of Life, Vol 1.</i> It was released in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> only. The song was successful, becoming Lil' Kim's third consecutive top 10 hit in Germany after her number 5 hit "Lady Marmalade."
</p><p>In 2002, Lil' Kim recorded a new entrance theme for then <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">World Wrestling Entertainment</a> (WWE) Women's Champion <a href="/wiki/Trish_Stratus" title="Trish Stratus">Trish Stratus</a> entitled "Time to Rock 'n Roll," which was used during broadcasts, until Stratus' retirement. The single was released on <i>WWE Anthology,</i> a compilation of entrance theme music to various <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> superstars.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim released the song "What's The Word" in mid-2002. Despite not having an official release, it went on to peak at number 9 on the <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Singles" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubbling Under R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles">Bubbling Under R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> It would later be released on the Japan edition of her third studio album, La Bella Mafia, as a bonus track.
</p>
<h3><span id="2003.E2.80.932005:_La_Bella_Mafia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003–2005:_La_Bella_Mafia">2003–2005: <i>La Bella Mafia</i></span></h3>
<p>On March 4, 2003, Lil' Kim released her third studio album, <i>La Bella Mafia.</i> It debuted at number 5 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling 166,000 copies in its first week,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> giving Lil' Kim her second consecutive top 5 album. The album received generally positive reviews from critics, receiving a score of 65 on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Buzz_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Buzz single">buzz single</a>, "Came Back For You," was released ahead of the album, the music video for the song featured reality television personality <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Gotti" title="Victoria Gotti">Victoria Gotti</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Jump_Off" title="The Jump Off">The Jump Off</a>," featuring <a href="/wiki/Mr._Cheeks" title="Mr. Cheeks">Mr. Cheeks</a>, peaked at number 16 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. Follow up single, "<a href="/wiki/Magic_Stick" title="Magic Stick">Magic Stick</a>," featuring 50 Cent, peaked at number two on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, staying there for three weeks. The song did not have a commercial release or a music video but was successful due to high radio airplay, peaking at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Airplay chart</a>. A third US-only single, "Thug Luv," featuring <a href="/wiki/Twista" title="Twista">Twista</a>, was released in the last quarter of 2003 and peaked at number 60 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs chart. The album was certified platinum in the US,<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> selling over 1.1 million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil' Kim promoted the album with a string of concerts, which also featured <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim was nominated for five Source Awards and won two ("Female Hip-Hop Artist of the Year," and "Female Single of the Year"). The album also got two Grammy Award nominations for Best Female Rap Solo Performance ("Came Back For You") and Best Rap Collaboration ("Magic Stick"). She was also nominated for Best Pop Collaboration with singer Christina Aguilera for the song "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Hold_Us_Down" title="Can&#39;t Hold Us Down">Can't Hold Us Down</a>," from Aguilera's album <i><a href="/wiki/Stripped_(Christina_Aguilera_album)" title="Stripped (Christina Aguilera album)">Stripped</a>.</i>
</p><p>Greg Thomas, an English professor at <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University" title="Syracuse University">Syracuse University</a>, began teaching "Hip-Hop Eshu: Queen B@#$H Lyricism 101." Lil' Kim herself was a guest speaker. Professor Thomas considered Lil' Kim's lyrics "the art with the most profound sexual politics I've ever seen anywhere."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Horowitz" title="David Horowitz">David Horowitz</a> criticized the course as "academic degeneracy and decline."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim also made an appearance on the multi-platform videogame <i><a href="/wiki/Def_Jam:_Fight_for_NY" title="Def Jam: Fight for NY">Def Jam: Fight for NY</a>.</i> Lil' Kim provided voice-overs for her part in the storyline, where the player may fight an opponent to have Lil' Kim as their girlfriend.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Lil' Kim recorded a cover of "<a href="/wiki/These_Boots_Are_Made_for_Walkin%27" title="These Boots Are Made for Walkin&#39;">These Boots Are Made for Walkin'</a>" which was used as the opening theme for Victoria Gotti's reality series <i><a href="/wiki/Growing_Up_Gotti" title="Growing Up Gotti">Growing Up Gotti</a>.</i> That same year, Lil' Kim was featured on the remix of "<a href="/wiki/Naughty_Girl_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Naughty Girl (Beyoncé song)">Naughty Girl</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>. In December 2004, Lil' Kim began recording a pilot for a <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> reality show titled <i>718 Makeover.</i><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The 718 in the title is the <a href="/wiki/Area_code_718" class="mw-redirect" title="Area code 718">area code</a> for Brooklyn, where she grew up. The show did not make it to air.
</p>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932008:_Prison.2C_The_Naked_Truth_and_Ms._G.O.A.T"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2008:_Prison,_The_Naked_Truth_and_Ms._G.O.A.T">2005–2008: Prison, <i>The Naked Truth</i> and <i>Ms. G.O.A.T</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg/220px-Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg/330px-Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg/440px-Lil%27_Kim_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="482" /></a><figcaption>Lil' Kim performing at Way Out West festival, 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>Lil' Kim released her fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Naked_Truth_(Lil%27_Kim_album)" title="The Naked Truth (Lil&#39; Kim album)">The Naked Truth</a>,</i> on September 27, 2005, while serving a federal prison sentence. It earned her a 5 mic rating from <i>The Source,</i> making her the only female rapper to ever receive a 5 mic rating. The album debuted at number 6 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart, selling 109,000 copies in its first week of release,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> giving Lil' Kim her third top 10 debut on the chart. <i>The Naked Truth</i> did not sell as well as her previous works, it only managed to reach a gold certification by <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a>. She said that her prison sentence left her with no time to promote the project.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for <i>The Naked Truth</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> first single, "<a href="/wiki/Lighters_Up" title="Lighters Up">Lighters Up</a>," was number one on <a href="/wiki/BET" title="BET">BET</a>'s <i>106 &amp; Park</i> for two weeks. "Lighters Up" was a Top Ten hit on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Singles_%26_Tracks" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles &amp; Tracks">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles &amp; Tracks</a> chart. The single also reached number 67 on the German Single Chart, number 12 on the UK Top 75 and number 4 on the Finland Single Chart. The second single, "Whoa" was released on February 17, 2006. It reached number 22 on Airplay.
</p><p>On March 9, 2006, BET premiered the show <i><a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim:_Countdown_to_Lockdown" title="Lil&#39; Kim: Countdown to Lockdown">Lil' Kim: Countdown to Lockdown</a>,</i> which was filmed before Lil' Kim headed to prison. The show became the highest rated premiere in BET history, averaging 1.9 million viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In May 2006, <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Debbie Harry</a> released a song in tribute to Lil' Kim called "Dirty and Deep" in protest of her conviction. The song was available for free from her official website. <i>Dance Remixes,</i> her first <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a>, was released on June 6, 2006. The album featured remixes of songs from <i>The Naked Truth</i> and <i>Hard Core.</i>
</p><p>A limited pressing released only in the US, it received no promotion, due to Lil' Kim being in prison at the time of release, and failed to chart. On August 31, 2006, Lil' Kim presented the award for Best Male Video at the <a href="/wiki/2006_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2006 MTV Video Music Awards">2006 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, it marked her first televised appearance since being released from prison.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> She also made appearances on the show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pussycat_Dolls_Present:_The_Search_for_the_Next_Doll" class="mw-redirect" title="The Pussycat Dolls Present: The Search for the Next Doll">The Pussycat Dolls Present: The Search for the Next Doll</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pussycat_Dolls_Present:_Girlicious" title="Pussycat Dolls Present: Girlicious">Pussycat Dolls Present: Girlicious</a></i> in 2007 and 2008 as a judge.
</p><p>In January 2008, Lil' Kim announced that she had parted ways with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>, choosing to release future projects independently. She stated she had no hard feelings toward Atlantic, but felt comfortable enough with her knowledge of the music business to do it alone.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim released her first <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ms._G.O.A.T." title="Ms. G.O.A.T.">Ms. G.O.A.T.</a>,</i> an <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> for "Greatest of All Time,"<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xp_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xp-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> on June 3, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-amg_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amg-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> It was produced by New York City DJs <a href="/wiki/Mister_Cee" title="Mister Cee">Mister Cee</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Whoo_Kid" title="DJ Whoo Kid">DJ Whoo Kid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gr_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gr-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Among critics, the mixtape received generally positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-dp_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dp-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ahh_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahh-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> It has been called a representation of Lil' Kim's return to the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Tito Salinas of <i>All Hip Hop</i> says "Lil' Kim shows that her time behind bars did not rust all of her swag away" on <i>Ms. G.O.A.T.</i><sup id="cite_ref-ahh_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahh-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, Ehren Gresehover of <i>New York Mag</i> says that although one of the tracks "The Miseducation of Lil' Kim" is not bad, he wished it was Lauryn Hill making a comeback instead.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932011:_Dancing_with_the_Stars_and_Black_Friday"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–2011:_Dancing_with_the_Stars_and_Black_Friday">2009–2011: <i>Dancing with the Stars</i> and <i>Black Friday</i></span></h3>
<p>On March 10, 2009, the song "Girls" by Korean singer <a href="/wiki/Seven_(Korean_singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven (Korean singer)">Seven</a> featuring Lil' Kim was released through digital stores as his U.S. debut single. Lil' Kim appeared in the music video that was released on the same day. "Girls" was produced by <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Darkchild</a>. On March 24, 2009, she released the song "<a href="/wiki/Download_(Lil%27_Kim_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Download (Lil&#39; Kim song)">Download</a>" featuring R&amp;B singers <a href="/wiki/T-Pain" title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Wilson_(singer)" title="Charlie Wilson (singer)">Charlie Wilson</a>. It was written by Lil' Kim and T-Pain and produced by Trackmasters. The song samples "Computer Love" by Zapp. Although it missed the Hot 100, it did chart on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs chart, peaking at number 21.
</p><p>Lil' Kim appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._season_8)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. season 8)">eighth season</a> of <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a>,</i> which began airing on March 9, 2009. She was paired with professional dancer <a href="/wiki/Derek_Hough" title="Derek Hough">Derek Hough</a>. They were eliminated on May 5, 2009, against <a href="/wiki/Ty_Murray" title="Ty Murray">Ty Murray</a> and his partner <a href="/wiki/Chelsie_Hightower" title="Chelsie Hightower">Chelsie Hightower</a>, putting Lil' Kim at fifth place among all thirteen contestants that season. Her elimination was met by many boos from the audience, as she was a consistent high-scorer and fan favorite.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 16, 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a> song "Hey Ho," which featured Lil' Kim and Lil Fate, was released as a promo single for his seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Sexes_(album)" title="Battle of the Sexes (album)">Battle of the Sexes</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In June 2010, Lil' Kim started her 2010 Tour, her first headlining tour since 2000. It took her across the US, as well as Canada and Europe.
</p><p>Lil' Kim released her second mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_(Lil%27_Kim_mixtape)" title="Black Friday (Lil&#39; Kim mixtape)">Black Friday</a>,</i> on February 14, 2011. The video for the title track was released on February 16, 2011. The mixtape received mostly negative reviews from critics. It was made available for purchase via <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>. In May 2011, Lil' Kim performed in South Africa as part of the music festival ZarFest alongside <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ciara" title="Ciara">Ciara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 19, 2011, Lil' Kim performed alongside G-Unit member <a href="/wiki/Shawty_Lo" title="Shawty Lo">Shawty Lo</a> and hinted a possible working relationship with <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Records" title="G-Unit Records">G-Unit Records</a>. That same month the song Lil' Kim, along with <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, was featured on titled "<a href="/wiki/Anything_(To_Find_You)" title="Anything (To Find You)">Anything (To Find You)</a>," by R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Monica_(singer)" title="Monica (singer)">Monica</a> was leaked. The song, which samples the Notorious B.I.G.'s "<a href="/wiki/Who_Shot_Ya%3F" title="Who Shot Ya?">Who Shot Ya?</a>," initially featured just Lil' Kim, but her second verse was removed to make room for Ross. Her vocals were then removed fully due to contractual issues with B.I.G.'s estate.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2011, Lil' Kim performed four dates in Australia as part of the WinterBeatz Festival alongside <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_(American_singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mario (American singer)">Mario</a>, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>. During the August, 17 date in Perth, she joined 50 Cent on stage for a performance of "Magic Stick." It marked the first time the pair had performed the song together.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On November 28, 2011, Lil' Kim released a <a href="/wiki/Promotional_recording" title="Promotional recording">buzz single</a> called "I Am Not the One." She also announced that she would release an EP, but it was later shelved for unknown reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932016:_Hard_Core_mixtape_and_Lil_Kim_Season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2016:_Hard_Core_mixtape_and_Lil_Kim_Season">2012–2016: <i>Hard Core</i> mixtape and <i>Lil Kim Season</i></span></h3>
<p>In the summer of 2011, Lil' Kim began recording material for her fifth studio album. She had previously been under a restriction banning her from releasing new material as a result of her settlement with Trackmasters, but it had now been lifted.<sup id="cite_ref-rapup_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapup-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wblk_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wblk-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-drewreports_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drewreports-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On Valentine's Day 2012, Lil' Kim released the song "If You Love Me" produced by Prince Saheb of <a href="/wiki/Knockout_Entertainment" title="Knockout Entertainment">Knockout Entertainment</a> as a gift to her fans. That same month it was announced she would make her return to the stage on <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rip_the_Runway" title="Rip the Runway">Rip the Runway</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It marked her first televised performance in years.
</p><p>In March 2012, during an interview with MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/Sucker_Free" title="Sucker Free">Sucker Free</a>,</i> Lil' Kim revealed that contract issues with production duo <a href="/wiki/Trackmasters" title="Trackmasters">Trackmasters</a> were the reason behind her album delay, saying ."..contractually, by the courts, I could not record any music – I wasn't supposed to put any music out."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On March 23, 2012, the song "Keys to the City," a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>, was leaked to the Internet. Lil' Kim first mentioned the song during an interview with MTV's RapFix, saying "I have a song with another celebrity person that I know the world and my fans are gonna love... It's vintage Kim mixed with the new Kim." During the same RapFix interview, Lil' Kim also revealed another song, titled "I'm Ready," which she hopes to do with rapper 50 Cent. Lil' Kim also commented on the direction of her music, saying she was in "Kanye West mode," adding ."..You do whatever you want to do ...it's all about taking chances."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim kicked off her <a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Queen_Tour" title="Return of the Queen Tour">Return of the Queen Tour</a> on May 17, 2012, to positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a radio interview at Miami's 99 Jamz, Lil' Kim stated that her book, <i>The Price of Loyalty,</i> was on hold to coincide with the release of her new album.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During an interview with <i>XXL</i> on April 26, 2013, she revealed that she does not have a name for the album yet, but the first official single would be out by mid year.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Kim described the single, produced by Bangladesh, as "different" and "sweet dessert."<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On July 11, 2013, Lil' Kim released the <a href="/wiki/Rockwilder" title="Rockwilder">Rockwilder</a>-produced single "Looks Like Money" as a free download for her fans on her birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 26, 2013, Lil' Kim announced and released the cover art for a new mixtape, <i>Hard Core 2K13,</i> which would also serve as a sequel to her critically acclaimed debut album, <i>Hard Core.</i><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was originally set to be released on October 31, 2013, but for then unknown reasons, was pushed back. To make up for not releasing the mixtape, Lil' Kim released the singles "Dead Gal Walking" and "Kimmy Blanco" to the public, along with the track list. The track list revealed collaborations with <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yo_Gotti" title="Yo Gotti">Yo Gotti</a>.
</p><p>On August 2, 2014, Lil' Kim announced via her Twitter page that she would launch a concert tour to promote her forthcoming <a href="/wiki/Hard_Core_(Lil%27_Kim_mixtape)" title="Hard Core (Lil&#39; Kim mixtape)"><i>Hard Core</i> Mixtape</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-twitter.com_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Throughout the remainder of August, Lil' Kim released a number of remixes to popular songs, including <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>'s and Nicki Minaj's collaboration on "Flawless," seemingly as a diss to Minaj, reigniting the feud between the two rappers.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 11, 2014, the <i>Hard Core</i> mixtape was released as free download on Kim's official website.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Revolt_(TV_network)" title="Revolt (TV network)">Revolt TV</a> on the same day, she revealed that she, Iggy Azalea, and T.I. would collaborate on a song sometime in the future, saying "I don't know if it's going to be for my album or if we're just going to…we have other plans for it as well. But, I think we're going to do a double release." In the same interview, she explained why the mixtape was pushed back twice, stating "When this project was supposed to come out I had got pregnant. I didn't know. [...] Once I became fully pregnant, I was working in the studio but at one point I couldn't work anymore, obviously."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, her fourth mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Lil_Kim_Season" title="Lil Kim Season">Lil Kim Season</a></i> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On the mixtape, she freestyles over several popular beats, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Summer_Sixteen" title="Summer Sixteen">Summer Sixteen</a>," <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Work_(Rihanna_song)" title="Work (Rihanna song)">Work</a>," and <a href="/wiki/Desiigner" title="Desiigner">Desiigner</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Panda_(Desiigner_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Panda (Desiigner song)">Panda</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It received mixed reviews from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Jen Yamato from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> wrote, "if anything, <i>Lil Kim Season</i> indicates that Kim's got her sights set on returning in a big way—and that she's collecting collaborators who might help her achieve it."<sup id="cite_ref-Yamato_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yamato-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.93present:_Girls_Cruise_and_9"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–present:_Girls_Cruise_and_9">2017–present: <i>Girls Cruise</i> and <i>9</i></span></h3>
<p>In February 2017, Lil' Kim announced via her Instagram and an interview that she was working on a new album.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Singer <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a> featured her on the song "Lovin You for Life" on the album <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_%26_I_(Faith_Evans_and_The_Notorious_B.I.G._album)" title="The King &amp; I (Faith Evans and The Notorious B.I.G. album)">The King &amp; I</a>,</i> released on May 19, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> That same month, Lil' Kim along with <a href="/wiki/Eve_(rapper)" title="Eve (rapper)">Eve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a> was featured on the remix of "I'm Better" by <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>.  In November, Lil' Kim released a promotional single "<a href="/wiki/Took_Us_a_Break" title="Took Us a Break">Took Us a Break</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and was featured on the song "<a href="/wiki/Wake_Me_Up_(Remy_Ma_song)" title="Wake Me Up (Remy Ma song)">Wake Me Up</a>" by rapper <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018, Lil' Kim released another promotional single, "Spicy," featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 11, 2018, Lil' Kim released the single "<a href="/wiki/Nasty_One" title="Nasty One">Nasty One</a>" from her highly anticipated album, but ultimately the track was not included on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> That same day during an interview with <i>Billboard,</i> she said the album would be released in November of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A remix for the single was released on October 26, 2018, and featured <a href="/wiki/Kranium" title="Kranium">Kranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/HoodCelebrityy" title="HoodCelebrityy">HoodCelebrityy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stefflon_Don" title="Stefflon Don">Stefflon Don</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tmz.com_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmz.com-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2018, she announced that the debut single for her album "Go Awff" would be released at a later date. The song was eventually released on February 15, 2019. That same month, Kim was spotted in Barbados with fellow hip hop stars <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BDa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mýa">Mýa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rozonda_Thomas" title="Rozonda Thomas">Chilli</a>, friends Char DeFrancesco (husband to <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a> and one of Kim's best friends) and Tiffany,  as well as  <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> personalities Pretty Vee and B. Simone from MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_%27n_Out" title="Wild &#39;n Out">Wild 'n Out</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-tmz.com_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmz.com-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was later revealed that this was part of a <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> reality show, <i><a href="/wiki/Girls_Cruise" title="Girls Cruise">Girls Cruise</a>,</i> for which Kim would serve as an executive producer. The show followed the group as they set sail to embark on a 10-day cruise in the Caribbean, visiting the countries of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> just in time for <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> festivities. It also documented the group's bonding and new friendships with one another. The show premiered on July 15 with approximately 1.2 million viewers and ran for 11 episodes. It is unclear if there will be another season of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2019, Kim revealed that her new album would be titled <a href="/wiki/9_(Lil%27_Kim_album)" title="9 (Lil&#39; Kim album)"><i>9</i></a> and added "There's a lot of meaning behind that." Later that month, she announced that the album would be released on May 17, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> After a minor setback with her record label, <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_One_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Entertainment One Music">eOne Music</a>, that caused the album not be released on the original planned date, the project was postponed. On September 27, 2019, Kim released a second single, "Found You," featuring <a href="/wiki/City_Girls" title="City Girls">City Girls</a> and <a href="/wiki/O.T._Genasis" title="O.T. Genasis">O.T. Genasis</a>. The album later became available for pre-order on all digital-download platforms on October 4, 2019 (along with the track "Pray For Me" featuring <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Musiq_Soulchild" title="Musiq Soulchild">Musiq Soulchild</a>), with a release date of October 11, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon its first week of release, the album charted on the R&amp;B/Hip-Hop and Rap Album Sales, Digital Albums, Top Albums Sales, Independent Albums and Rap Album Sales.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> However, the album failed to chart on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 due to selling less than 1,000 copies, and no song from the album landed on the Hot 100 or Bubbling Under.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> During one of the reunion episodes for <i>Girls Cruise,</i> Kim revealed that the album would be a two-part project, stating "I recorded so many songs. I have a part one and a part two." She also shared that her co-star, the Instagram comedian Vena "Pretty Vee" Excell, would appear on the record.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2019, Kim revealed that she would collaborate with <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Hilton" title="Paris Hilton">Paris Hilton</a> on the follow-up to <i>9.</i><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with New York Radio 103.9, Kim confirmed that the <a href="/wiki/City_Girls" title="City Girls">City Girls</a> would be involved with the follow-up to <i>9.</i> She also stated that she would "love" to have Pretty Vee host her tour.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> On her November 8, 2019 appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Real_(talk_show)" title="The Real (talk show)">The Real</a>,</i> Kim again confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Paris_Hilton" title="Paris Hilton">Paris Hilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> would appear on <i>9</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s follow-up; she said the song "sounds like a classic Missy Elliott record but 'now.'"(1:20<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h2>
<p>Lil' Kim cited as her rap influences <a href="/wiki/MC_Lyte" title="MC Lyte">MC Lyte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt-N-Pepa" title="Salt-N-Pepa">Salt-N-Pepa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roxanne_Shant%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Roxanne Shanté">Roxanne Shanté</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> She was also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_B._%26_Rakim" title="Eric B. &amp; Rakim">Eric B. &amp; Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>. Lil' Kim also cited <a href="/wiki/Madonna" title="Madonna">Madonna</a> as an influence, saying she modeled her own career on Madonna's, and labeling herself as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Black Madonna</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_endorsements">Products and endorsements</span></h2>
<p>In 1998, Lil' Kim signed with <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_Models" title="Wilhelmina Models">Wilhelmina Models</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> That same year she was announced as the face for the fashion brand <a href="/wiki/Candie%27s" title="Candie&#39;s">Candie's</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>. She became the first and only rapper to endorse the brand to date. In 2000, Lil' Kim signed a deal with fashion house <a href="/wiki/Iceberg_(fashion_house)" title="Iceberg (fashion house)">Iceberg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and also with cosmetics brand <a href="/wiki/MAC_Cosmetics" title="MAC Cosmetics">MAC</a> to help endorse their VIVA GLAM line of lipsticks and lip glosses alongside <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The MAC <i>VIVA GLAM III</i> campaign, which was built around a plum-brown lipstick, helped raise $4 million for the company in one year and became the most successful VIVA GLAM campaign to date.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Due to the success, the two signed on for a second year. The rapper also modeled for the urban fashion line Baby Phat in August 2000. In March 2001, Lil' Kim, along with several other artists, were in an <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/Mac_(computer)" title="Mac (computer)">Mac</a> computer commercial, demonstrating how to burn custom CDs on a Mac.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004 she launched a designer watch collection with manufacturer and jeweler Jeweler <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Arabo" title="Jacob Arabo">Jacob Arabo</a>, <i>Royalty by Lil' Kim.</i><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> She also debuted her first clothing line, <i>Hollyhood.</i><sup id="cite_ref-MTVarticle_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVarticle-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> She lent her voice to the video game <i>Def Jam: Fight for NY,</i> in which she was featured.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 shecollaborated on a shoe line with high-end brand Petite Peton. That same year she appeared as a character in the limited-edition comic book "The Heist," a collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel</a> and Atlantic Records.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010, Lil' Kim signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Three_Olives_Vodka" title="Three Olives Vodka">Three Olives Vodka</a> as the face for their <i>Purple</i> vodka.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In September of that same year, she, along with her cousin Katrise Jones, opened their first beauty salon in Charlotte, North Carolina called <i>Salon Se Swa.</i><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> That same month she launched her second clothing line, <i>24/7 Goddess Collection,</i> at Charlotte, North Carolina's Fashion Week.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, Lil' Kim began endorsing <a href="/wiki/C%C3%AEroc" title="Cîroc">Cîroc</a> vodka, revealing her own cocktail, "Queen Bee," and announcing herself as the "First Lady" of the brand.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h2>
<p>In 2000, Lil' Kim embarked on a promo tour for her second studio album, <i>The Notorious K.I.M.,</i> and the <a href="/wiki/MAC_AIDS_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="MAC AIDS Fund">MAC AIDS Fund</a>. She visited MAC cosmetics counters, interacted with fans, and helped raise money and awareness for people living with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> She took part in MAC's <i>Fashion Cares</i> show in Toronto, Canada, raising close to one million for its AIDS committee.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Her endorsement of MAC, with Mary J. Blige, raised $4 million for the fund.
</p><p>In October 2001, Lil' Kim was featured on the R&amp;B mix of the song "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_Going_On_(song)" title="What&#39;s Going On (song)">What's Going On</a>." She, along with several other popular recording artists, released the song as "Artists Against AIDS Worldwide," with proceeds going to AIDS programs worldwide and also the <a href="/wiki/September_11th_Fund" title="September 11th Fund">September 11th Fund</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Way" title="United Way">United Way</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> That same month, Lil' Kim performed at Breathe, a benefit concert for breast cancer research and treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Proceeds from the concert went to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">UCLA</a> Breast Center and the Breast Examination Center of Harlem, an outreach program of the <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan_Kettering_Cancer_Center" title="Memorial Sloan Kettering Cancer Center">Memorial Sloan Kettering Cancer Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 12, 2002, Lil' Kim walked her dogs in the 3rd annual "Paws for Style" fashion show. The event is held by <a href="/wiki/Animal_Fair_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal Fair (magazine)"><i>Animal Fair</i> magazine</a> as a benefit for the <a href="/wiki/Humane_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Humane Society">Humane Society</a> of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Items worn by the animals were later auctioned off online.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In 2004 she launched her own foundation called <i>Lil' Kim Cares.</i><sup id="cite_ref-MTVarticle_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVarticle-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The foundation raises funds, resources and awareness for national programs that assist with issues such as homelessness, HIV/AIDS prevention and awareness, transitional living, child neglect, and violence against women.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Speaking of the foundation, Lil' Kim stated she planned to be primarily involved in causes that had affected her personally.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On April 17, 2004, she participated in the 28th annual <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Pro/Celebrity_Race" title="Toyota Pro/Celebrity Race">Toyota Pro/Celebrity Race</a>. The event helped raise more than $100,000 for "Racing for Kids," a non-profit program benefiting Southern California children's hospitals in Long Beach and Orange County.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> On August 24, 2004, Lil' Kim encouraged others to vote in the <a href="/wiki/2004_United_States_presidential_election" title="2004 United States presidential election">United States presidential election</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Rock_the_Vote" title="Rock the Vote">Rock the Vote</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 10, 2005, Lil' Kim, along with several other artists, appeared in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apprentice_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Apprentice (U.S. TV series)">The Apprentice</a>.</i> Each artist was approached by contestants to donate a "personal experience" to be auctioned off for charity through music channel <a href="/wiki/Fuse_(TV_channel)" title="Fuse (TV channel)">Fuse</a>'s "Daily Download" program, with proceeds going to the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Glaser_Pediatric_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation">Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In September 2005, she teamed with <a href="/wiki/Fashion_design" title="Fashion design">fashion designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a> for a limited edition T-shirt line featuring images of the rapper. <i>Marc Jacobs Loves Lil' Kim</i> was sold exclusively at Marc Jacobs stores, with 100% of the proceeds going to a charity called The Door.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005 Lil' Kim donated a diamond watch from her "Royalty" line to the <a href="/wiki/World_AIDS_Day" title="World AIDS Day">World AIDS Day</a> eBay auction, "Bid 2 Beat AIDS." Proceeds went to LIFEbeat, an organization providing HIV/AIDS information to millions of young people annually.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Through her foundation, Lil' Kim has given back to many, including teaming up with apparel company <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_%26_Ness" title="Mitchell &amp; Ness">Mitchell &amp; Ness</a> and boxer <a href="/wiki/Zab_Judah" title="Zab Judah">Zab Judah</a> to donate toys to underprivileged youth in Philadelphia in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and joining <a href="/wiki/MusiCares" title="MusiCares">MusiCares</a> in 2007 for a silent auction, held at the <i>Grammys On The Hill</i> ceremony, to help raise funds for the foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007 Lil' Kim was a part of the <i>4th Annual Grammy Charity Holiday Auction,</i> featuring a large variety of celebrity-signed memorabilia that people could bid on through <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> On December 1, 2007, Lil' Kim partnered with Preserve Our Legacy and the New Jersey Stem Cell Research and Education Foundation to host a celebrity basketball game to raise awareness about various health issues plaguing minority communities.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 11, 2010, Lil' Kim launched her signature milkshake, the "Queen Bee," at Millions of Milkshakes in West Hollywood, with proceeds going towards <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9le_Haiti_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Yéle Haiti Foundation">Yéle Haiti Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> On February 9, 2013, she took part in the first annual <i>Reality On The Runway</i> fashion show. The event helped raise $300,000 for people infected with HIV/AIDS and increase awareness. All designs from the show were auctioned off online following the event, with a portion of the proceeds going to AIDS United.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil' Kim has been a longtime <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT rights">LGBT advocate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-pride_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pride-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and has participated in many <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride_festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gay pride festival">gay pride festivals</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/LGBT_Pride_March_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT Pride March (New York City)">LGBT Pride March</a> in New York City, as well as performing at <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Black_Pride" title="Atlanta Black Pride">Atlanta Black Pride</a> and <a href="/wiki/D.C._Black_Pride" title="D.C. Black Pride">D.C. Black Pride</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pride_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pride-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In her teens, Jones dated Shawn Powell. The pair met at the Empire Roller Skating rink in Brooklyn. After a couple of months of seeing each other, Powell was arrested for robbery and sentenced to eight and a half years in prison. Jones and Powell continued their relationship, with Jones visiting frequently. They kept in touch by writing letters. The couple became engaged while Powell was incarcerated.<sup id="cite_ref-Driven_ep_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Driven_ep-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During this time, Jones met Christopher Wallace (The Notorious B.I.G.). She focused starting her rap career, called off the engagement with Powell, and the couple split.<sup id="cite_ref-Driven_ep_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Driven_ep-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, during the recording of her debut album, Jones became pregnant with Wallace's child.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> She did not make it public until 1999 during an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source" title="The Source">The Source</a>.</i> Jones decided to terminate the pregnancy. "I already knew the kind of relationship that Biggie and I had, and I knew that [having a child] was something that couldn't take place..."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wallace called Jones three days before his death and told her he loved her.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In a 2010 interview with <a href="/wiki/Ed_Lover" title="Ed Lover">Ed Lover</a> on <a href="/wiki/WWPR-FM" title="WWPR-FM">Power 105</a>, Jones revealed that Wallace assaulted her and she described an incident where he choked her to unconsciousness.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Jones admitted her relationship with Wallace was "very violent" after <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a> claimed that he witnessed Wallace pull a pistol out on Jones.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 23, 1996, Jones was arrested for possession of <a href="/wiki/Marijuana" class="mw-redirect" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> after police raided Wallace's Teaneck, New Jersey home. Police smelled marijuana inside the home when they went to ask for someone to move an illegally parked car. Jones denied she was smoking, claiming she was "upstairs all day sleeping."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On March 17, 1999, Teaneck police issued an arrest warrant after Jones failed to turn up for court dates stemming from the arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The warrant was not a top priority for the police, and was not made public until September 2003, after a story was published online by <a href="/wiki/The_Smoking_Gun" title="The Smoking Gun">The Smoking Gun</a>. Jones was later removed from Teaneck's wanted list in October 2003, after $350 in bail was posted on her behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Jones' attorney told reporters that she did not appear in court because she believed the case had been resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, Jones started dating Damion "World" Hardy. The couple split in 2003, and she stated she was a victim of physical abuse leading to multiple nose jobs as a result of being punched.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 20, 2003, Jones had $250,000 worth of jewelry stolen while catching a flight at New York's <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> after a bag, which she intended to <a href="/wiki/Hand_luggage" title="Hand luggage">carry on</a>, was mixed up with eight other pieces of her luggage.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The missing jewelry was recovered 10 days later, found wrapped up in a rag in a locker room for airline employees by a United Airlines worker.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Jones dated record producer <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>, whom she met when he offered her a ride to her hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-scott_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scott-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The couple split after two months.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Storch revealed that he would have married Jones if the relationship had worked out.<sup id="cite_ref-scott_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scott-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Jones and <a href="/wiki/Ray_J" title="Ray J">Ray J</a> briefly dated.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 17, 2005, Lil' Kim was convicted of three counts of <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspiracy</a> and one count of <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> for lying to a federal <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">grand jury</a> about her and her friends' involvement in a 2001 shooting outside the <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> studios in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> During the trial of her co-manager, Damion "D-Roc" Butler, and her bodyguard, Suif "Gutta" Jackson, a former member of the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> group Junior M.A.F.I.A., she testified before a grand jury that she did not know they were at the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodyguard_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodyguard-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> However, video footage from a security camera placed all three at the scene, exiting the building.<sup id="cite_ref-Released_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Released-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Butler and Jackson pleaded guilty to gun charges. Jackson was sentenced to twelve years in federal prison as part of plea bargain in which he admitted to firing at least twenty rounds during the incident. The length of the sentence was said to have been influenced by his previous gun-related convictions.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodyguard_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodyguard-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2005, Lil' Kim was sentenced to one year in prison, thirty days' home detention upon release from custody, and three years of probation. She served the entirety of her sentence at the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Detention_Center,_Philadelphia" title="Federal Detention Center, Philadelphia">Federal Detention Center, Philadelphia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Center_City,_Philadelphia" title="Center City, Philadelphia">Center City, Philadelphia</a>. She was released on July 3, 2006, after serving approximately 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-Released_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Released-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Prisons" title="Federal Bureau of Prisons">Federal Bureau of Prisons</a> (BOP) supervision ended on August 2, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 9, 2014, Jones gave birth to a daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jones identifies as a Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feuds">Feuds</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foxy_Brown">Foxy Brown</span></h3>
<p>Once high school friends, Lil' Kim and Foxy Brown originally remained close despite becoming associates of clashing hip hop groups Junior M.A.F.I.A. and <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)" title="The Firm (hip hop group)">The Firm</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-vibe_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 1995, they collaborated with Da Brat for the remix of  "<a href="/wiki/No_One_Else_(Total_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="No One Else (Total song)">No One Else</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Total_(group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Total (group)">Total</a>. The following year, they were featured in the Hot 97 NY Fashion Show<sup id="cite_ref-hot97_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hot97-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and appeared on the covers of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source" title="The Source">The Source</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-bet_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bet-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> However, their first dispute developed after both of their debut studio albums were scheduled for release a week apart in November 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-bet_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bet-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
